  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3a5076e0-1ffa-48a5-9e17-46860bece5fa'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer15258833983013229772"><i>Reality, it turns out, is often not what you perceive it to be—sometimes, there really is someone out to get you. Made You Up tells the story of Alex, a high school senior unable to tell the difference between real life and delusion. This is a compelling and provoking literary debut that will appeal to fans of Wes Anderson, <b>Silver Linings Playbook</b> and <b>Liar</b>.</i><br/><br/>Alex fights a da</span>
  <span id="freeText15258833983013229772" style="display:none"><i>Reality, it turns out, is often not what you perceive it to be—sometimes, there really is someone out to get you. Made You Up tells the story of Alex, a high school senior unable to tell the difference between real life and delusion. This is a compelling and provoking literary debut that will appeal to fans of Wes Anderson, <b>Silver Linings Playbook</b> and <b>Liar</b>.</i><br /><br />Alex fights a daily battle to figure out the difference between reality and delusion. Armed with a take-no-prisoners attitude, her camera, a Magic 8-Ball, and her only ally (her little sister), Alex wages a war against her schizophrenia, determined to stay sane long enough to get into college. She’s pretty optimistic about her chances until classes begin, and she runs into Miles. Didn't she imagine him? Before she knows it, Alex is making friends, going to parties, falling in love, and experiencing all the usual rites of passage for teenagers. But Alex is used to being crazy. She’s not prepared for normal. <br /><br /><i>Funny, provoking, and ultimately moving, this debut novel featuring the quintessential unreliable narrator will have readers turning the pages and trying to figure out what is real and what is made up.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15258833983013229772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/21315471-stenedria"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1375580974i/21315471._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/21315471-stenedria">Stenedria</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I have a feeling it's real. Like what Miles says in the book, he has to be real since he is impacting others around him--not just Alex. Others see him<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I have a feeling it's real. Like what Miles says in the book, he has to be real since he is impacting others around him--not just Alex. Others see him, talk to him, interact with him. All of his actions (his existence in general) is real. I'm really glad the book was written that way instead of a plot twist where he really was made up. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<a href="/questions/1111151-can-someone-explain-the-lobster-bit-i">can someone explain the lobster bit? i didnt get it</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1111151'><a id="like_count_community_question_1111151" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1111151?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F17661416-made-you-up">like</a></span>

<a href="/questions/1111151-can-someone-explain-the-lobster-bit-i">3 years ago</a>

<a href="/questions/1111151-can-someone-explain-the-lobster-bit-i">Add your answer</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5386691"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1549300059i/5386691._UX100_CR0,38,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5386691">=^._.^=</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think she saw herself as the lobster. In the end of the book she mentions that Miles got out of the tank and she didn't, so in a way she is still as<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think she saw herself as the lobster. In the end of the book she mentions that Miles got out of the tank and she didn't, so in a way she is still asking for help or waiting for someone to help her. She would always do references to how the lobsters were in the tank like if the reason why they would pile together was because they were cold or just wanted to be there for each other and that's how she felt like when she was with Miles, or something metaphorical like that.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1251272315" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1251272315" />
    <a title="Clementine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31037758-clementine"><img alt="Clementine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419176916p2/31037758.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1251272315?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clementine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clementine" href="/user/show/31037758-clementine">Clementine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31037758-clementine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31037758-clementine?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31037758-clementine?shelf=love-vs-hatred-clich%C3%A9">love-vs-hatred-cliché</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31037758-clementine?shelf=thrown-out-the-window">thrown-out-the-window</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31037758-clementine?shelf=author-didn-t-research">author-didn-t-research</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31037758-clementine?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31037758-clementine?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31037758-clementine?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31037758-clementine?shelf=lost-my-eyeballs-rolling-my-eyes">lost-my-eyeballs-rolling-my-eyes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31037758-clementine?shelf=insensitive-mess">insensitive-mess</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1251272315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer411338349851743459">Oh well, look at that! I created a new shelve just for this book: 0-star. <br/><br/><b>It disgusts me that an author would use all the symptoms of schizophrenia that seem "glamorous", "sensationalist" or ask for angst with so much as no regard for accuracy. It disgusts me that because of authors like that, people are clapping their hands, thinking this is accurate and sensitive while it is not. <br/><br/>In fact, it's so disgustingly inaccurate that I could use this book any time to give one of my professors or collea</b></span>
  <span id="freeText411338349851743459" style="display:none">Oh well, look at that! I created a new shelve just for this book: 0-star. <br><br><b>It disgusts me that an author would use all the symptoms of schizophrenia that seem "glamorous", "sensationalist" or ask for angst with so much as no regard for accuracy. It disgusts me that because of authors like that, people are clapping their hands, thinking this is accurate and sensitive while it is not. <br><br>In fact, it's so disgustingly inaccurate that I could use this book any time to give one of my professors or colleague a heart attack. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436638993ra/15487635.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>This is the pop YA version of every movie wrongly depicting schizophrenia out there. This book is one of the reasons I spend so much of my time going to high schools and giving conferences about mental illness and the awareness that should go with it. This book is one of the reasons stigma against mentally ill people persist in society; because authors don't sit on their goddamn ass and fucking research like they are expected to.</i></b><br><br>So yeah: <b>**Actual rating: 0 star.**</b><br><br>Fuck this book, seriously.<br><br>I wish I could sit here and do a coherent review of what went wrong and where with detailed analysis of the plot and characters, but this is not my main issue with this book. Yes, I thought the plot was a patchwork of "angsty" events that weren’t handled with the sensitivity that would normally be required. Yes, I thought the child molesting subplot was just there to give a drive to the novel and it disgusts me but I’m afraid I don’t have enough caracters to explain fully how it shocks me that everyone is giving this raving reviews. Yes, I was personally insulted that a character’s French accent is used as comic relief when Miles spends so much time telling Alex how bullied he was because of his German accent: "Oh, look she can pronounce her "th", let’s spell it out for readers." Yes, the brain trauma bit is inaccurate: if she had been unconscious for three days, she would have severe brain trauma and axonal loss, so neurological problems. But that too was just a subplot, so she walked out of the hospital the next day. And the father beating the shit out of his wife and kid? Another disgusting subplot. Another stone toward happily ever after that is mandatory to all YA contemporary book.<br><br><b>
  <i>Fuck this book, seriously.</i>
</b><br><br>I’m a psychologist in training. I don’t want to talk about plot and characters and the lack of diversity in this novel, I want to talk about schizophrenia.<br><br>Top twelve "You know nothing, Jon Snow, about schizophrenia" clues Francesca Zappia style:<br><br>1-<b>You use interchangeably delusions and hallucinations.</b> Delusions refer to beliefs. Patients with schizophrenia would then be convinced of something; their own invincibility or that if they do things a certain way they won’t be in danger for example. It’s not part of a hallucination, even less a hallucination per say like it’s depicted in the novel. Hallucinations and delusions are two VERY different things and the fact that the author uses them as synonyms shows the lack of research she has put in her novel. <br><br>2-<b>You think the worst thing that could happen with antipsychotics is nausea when you eat.</b> Excuse you, but had you done your job, you would know that secondary effects are in fact nasty when it comes to antipsychotics. Some patients develop extrapyramidal symptoms which is just the fancy medical way to say that their movements will become jerky and Parkinson-like. The secondary effects are less heavy for the pills of the second generation, yes, but if you’re just nauseous, you’re lucky. One more thing: if you’re not taking your pills, you are going through withdrawal symptoms. But we will get to that in the next item. <br><br>3-<b>You think it’s healthy to force someone to take their medication while being unsure whether they took it or not previously.</b> Fuck NO! NEVER EVER force someone to take their pills when you’re not sure wether they have taken them or not. (I can assure you that the patient missing her intakes would feel it in her body, but hey the mom in this book looks like she knows so much better.) They could have a toxic reaction to the pills because unlike most drugs antipsychotics must be entirely metabolized before being eliminated from the body. That’s why, we are extremely conservative when it comes to when they take their pills. Not a fucking walk in the park. We don’t shit around with this. The secondary effects list is longer than my arms so if the molecules is accumulated in the organism, it could get worse. So DON’T DO THAT! <br><br>4-<b>You think visual hallucinations are fairly common in schizophrenia.</b> Big LOLZ to that. So the big twist? BIG FUCKING BULLSHIT! SENSATIONALISM! That’s what it is: SENSATIONALISM because it has NOTHING to do with schizophrenia. Visual hallucinations are the rarest form of hallucinations in the general population. They occur more often in patients of African descent. Caucasian with visual hallucinations that began at the age of 7? Nein. Non. No. Auditory hallucinations are much more common. And even if let’s say, Alex is the one in one million who is the special snowflake of the bunch and she has the rare occurrence of child manifestation on top of the visual hallucinations rarity: hallucinations affect one sensory pattern at a time. Alex has a hallucination that affects her vision, her sense of smell and her touch all at once... NO. That’s not how it works. Stop. It. (And a psychosis episode that went on for four years?... Huh. No.)<br><br>5-<b>You decided that it didn’t matter that female patients’ symptoms appear in their twenties.</b> Female patients present symptoms after male patients. <i>But big LOL to that cuz this YA, yo, and we needed angst, right? So fuck science. Fuck how many female patients take this mental illness harder since they either have children and a husband and/or a career when they are diagnosed. But, hey, why comment on that when you could have a love story with a jerk? Bonus point if she says things like: "I didn’t care about perimeter checks anymore". Cuz this is YA, yo.</i> Inaccurate and love cures it all. FUCK. THAT. Even if Alex had been a minor with symptoms that resembled schizophrenia, I personally know no one that would have made that diagnostic. 1) Because she’s a child and her brain is growing. 2) The schizophrenia diagnostic is something that brands you for life, so we don’t give it lightly. 3) Because her brain hasn’t matured completely, she could in fact be bipolar or have a personality disorder of Cluster A or be on drugs or have brain cancer, or just never develop schizophrenia. But I will get to that in the next item. 4) From what I read from her symptoms a.k.a "hallucinations and that’s it", I would have never given the diagnostic of schizophrenia. It takes more 2 or more symptoms of criteria A: delusions, disorganized speech, hallucinations, grossly disorganized or catatonic behaviour and negative symptoms. <i>Suddenly less glamorous, right?</i> And in all diagnostics, it must be showed that the disorder impacts personal functioning. None of that here. <br><br>6- <b>You don’t know shit about a schizophrenic brain.</b> Patients with schizophrenia have enlarged ventricles (the 1st and 2nd), that means their brain weighs less than a patient without schizophrenia. <b>
  <i>There’s up to 25% significantly less grey matter in certain areas in patients with schizophrenia.</i>
</b> They miss cortical grey matter in the temporal and frontal regions which are responsible for emotions and memory and language and other cognitive functions. But of course, Alex being the snow flake of schizophrenia that she is, she has no problem with the expression of emotions or memory or language and shows no sign of cognitive impairment. Usually, there is impairment in verbal memory and information processing. There’s also impairment in planning and decision making because it touches the prefrontal cortex. Of course, this doesn’t concern Alex, our dear snow flake. Because an Alex with disorganized speech or behaviour would simply wouldn’t be as glamorous, huh? Oh, we will get to that in the next item.<br><br>7-<b>You completely ignore the existence of negative symptoms because you think hallucinations make for a better more angsty show.</b> Negative symptoms appear often and they are: the absence of motivation and the absence of volition, poor speech and affective flattening. Antipsychotics treat only positive symptoms (that’s hallucinations and delusions), so usually all that remains are negative symptoms, also called residual symptoms. But there’s none of that here. <i>Cuz why go with symptoms that occur in general when you can have a snow-flake?</i><br><br>8-<b>You say « Fuck the therapist » whenever you can.</b> We don’t speak to parents the way it is depicted in the novel. We don’t because we have a therapeutic relationship with the child and we don’t want this to become a problem for the mother/father-son/daughter relationship or our own relationship with the patient. I have studied psychology for almost five years now. I think I know my hood, but a full-blown psychologist? They fucking own my hood. So stop. Seriously. We are here to help our patients not go behind their back and have them interned. (Oh and by the way? We don’t intern patients. This isn’t 1900, we don’t do that anymore.) It bugs me that every time the therapist is mentioned it’s through the mother’s mouth: "I’m calling your therapist." Like no. That’s not how it works. We work with the child, not with you, mom. Oh, and when it comes to medication? We evaluate often. If your medications don’t work, we adjust the dose or switch them. The fact that Alex has a therapist who doesn’t consider that her meds aren’t working after A WHOLE YEAR is so fucking inaccurate, I can’t even. But I will get to that in the next item. <br><br>9-<b>You don’t know that because adherence to treatment is hard in schizophrenic patients that we actually give them an injection every two weeks instead of giving them pills.</b> Everything I just said. Oh and "maybe she can consider a stronger medication?" that the mom mentioned to Alex without asking the therapist first? That’s not how it works. There’s no such thing as "stronger" meds, just meds that affect other neurotransmitters but this is getting long, so if you want me to tell you the difference between dopamine and serotonin just PM me. (Zappia, please PM me.)<br><br>10-<b>You know nothing about mental hospitals.</b> Deinstitutionalization. Look it up.<br><br>11- <b>You think after a minimum of 8 years of formation, we can mistake domestic violence for suicidal behaviour.</b> The worse part is: you think we would internalize a suicidal patient for YEARS. <i>Funny, how many subplots don’t work because the author did her research on the corner of a breakfast table between two bites. Hahahaha. Not.</i> Again and urgently: Deinstitutionalization. Look it up. Oh and look up domestic violence too, because that leaves marks that cannot be self-inflicted. Just saying.<br><br>12-<b>You think "subtypes" of schizophrenia are still used in diagnostic because paranoia makes for a better more angsty show.</b> The reason we don't use subtypes anymore to describe schizophrenia when giving our diagnostic is because more often than not, subtypes showed up together in patients. We were told "use the principal one", but it was VERY, VERY rarely that easy, cut on the line. Mixed-subtypes were the norms so since May 2013, we don't use them anymore. DSM-V, look it up.<br><br>Now excuse me when I go take another shower.<br><br>P.S.: If you want sources, PM me. (Zappia, please PM me.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="411338349851743459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1114337349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114337349" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1114337349?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1114337349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11894730220218841829"><i>
  <b>“Sometimes I think people take reality for granted.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>I stand by my earlier claim - YA contemporary is where it's at this year. I thought this book was excellent. Compelling, addictive, really weird and excellent. It was such an unusual novel; I can personally say I've never read anything quite like it and it's a great book for discussion. Such an unreliable narrator, constantly blurring the lines between reality and hallucination.<br/><br/>Alex suffers from paranoia and schizophrenia. Her world is full</span>
  <span id="freeText11894730220218841829" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“Sometimes I think people take reality for granted.”</b>
</i><br /><br />I stand by my earlier claim - YA contemporary is where it's at this year. I thought this book was excellent. Compelling, addictive, really weird and excellent. It was such an unusual novel; I can personally say I've never read anything quite like it and it's a great book for discussion. Such an unreliable narrator, constantly blurring the lines between reality and hallucination.<br /><br />Alex suffers from paranoia and schizophrenia. Her world is full of colours, objects, people and noises that may or may not really be there. She cannot trust her own senses, so she takes pictures of the world around her, knowing that any hallucinations will eventually fade and the reality will be left behind in the image. <b>And I just loved the way the story unfolded.</b><br /><br />See, years ago, Alex was first diagnosed when she recounted an incident that no one else seemed to think happened that way. Despite being haunted by this strange false memory, she always told herself that it was part of her mental illness and she had to accept that her memory was lying. Only... then she meets Miles and she begins to wonder if everything about that day was in her head, or if maybe there's something more to the story.<br /><br />It's fascinating. <b>You don't know what's real and what isn't.</b> The exploration of the line between reality and imagination kept me turning pages at a crazy pace to find out the truth. And it's such a charming little read with a cast of diverse and interesting characters. The dialogue is engaging and witty, without feeling strained like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1406384.John_Green" title="John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">John Green</a>'s sometimes does. <br /><br />I think I liked Alex and Miles because they're both kind of unlikable. Hehe. Alex is moody and antisocial; Miles is a total pain in the ass. But the weird relationship between them made me like them and made me care about them both. The story predictably takes the romantic route, but it happens very gradually and feels like a natural progression. Not the slightest whiff of insta-anything.<br /><br />Very enjoyable and very unique (at least to me). Highly recommended to all fans of YA contemporary.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11894730220218841829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1085543232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1085543232" />
    <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always"><img alt="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562987681p2/5478965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1085543232?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always">Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=i-think-my-heart-stopped">i-think-my-heart-stopped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=did-not-see-that-coming">did-not-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=holy-shit-that-ending">holy-shit-that-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=might-make-you-shit-bricks">might-make-you-shit-bricks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=swoony-book-boys">swoony-book-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=i-ugly-cried">i-ugly-cried</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085543232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5275565504205183970">6 Things That You Will Love About Made You Up + A Note to Francesca Zappia<br/><br/>1.) <strong>
  The absolutely charming heroine, Alex
</strong>. We have another unreliable narrator here, which I absolutely loved. But being unreliable isn't a reason not to connect with her. In fact, it was so incredibly easy for me to love her. <strong>Alex was sassy and sarcastic, but also troubled and with a lot of depth.</strong> To say that she had a strong personality would be an understatement.<br/><br/>2.) <strong>
  All of the <em>feelings</em>
</strong>. This book was so emotiona</span>
  <span id="freeText5275565504205183970" style="display:none">6 Things That You Will Love About Made You Up + A Note to Francesca Zappia<br /><br />1.) <strong>
  The absolutely charming heroine, Alex
</strong>. We have another unreliable narrator here, which I absolutely loved. But being unreliable isn't a reason not to connect with her. In fact, it was so incredibly easy for me to love her. <strong>Alex was sassy and sarcastic, but also troubled and with a lot of depth.</strong> To say that she had a strong personality would be an understatement.<br /><br />2.) <strong>
  All of the <em>feelings</em>
</strong>. This book was so emotionally engaging. I swooned (because hello, adorable romance), cried (yep. LEGIT TEARS), laughed (Alex's snark is just hilarious), and <em>felt all the feels</em>.<strong> It was easy to sympathize <em>and</em> empathize with Alex</strong>.<br /><br />3.)
  <strong> The schizophrenia</strong>
. I don't have schizophrenia or know anyone who suffers from it, but I have read a handful of books with main characters who have this mental illness. <em>Made You Up</em> was a lot different and was a breath of fresh air. <strong>I also loved how Alex seemed to already come to terms with her disease, and also how she still pushed through and made mature decisions about it in the end</strong>.<br /><br />4.) 
  <strong>The super adorable and <em>asdfghjkl</em> romance</strong>
. Miles is not the kind of guy you fall for instantly. At first he was closed off to the world, but as he opens up to Alex, you start to fall for him just as Alex was. <strong>It took time to progress (slow-burn romances are my favorites, as you know), and once it was there I was shipping these two <em>so hard</em> it hurt</strong>.<br /><br />5.)
  <strong> The supportive and loving family</strong>
. Alex could always count on her little sister Charlie for everything, and I loved them together. I also really want to say something here but <em>no spoilers</em>! Alex's parents weren't a prominent part of the story, but when they were there, you could easily see how much they loved their daughter and how much they didn't want to hurt her.<br /><br />6.) <strong>
  The crazy twists and the ending
</strong>. You'd expect that being a contemporary novel, you'll be able to see things coming from a mile away. WRONG.<strong> <em>Made You Up</em> had some intense twists that made me go <em>HOLY SHIT!</em> and want to curl up into a ball forever</strong>. Also the ending was unexpected and not your typical HEA, but it really worked. I thought it was an excellent way to end the book.<br /><br />Also, a quick note to Francesca Zappia:<strong> If you end up writing a mini epilogue to Made You Up, I will love you forever.</strong> And even if you don't, I'd pretty much read anything you'd write at this point. This book ended fantastically, but I want more! No pressure.<br /><br />Actual rating: <b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />Blog | <a href="http://iadorkyou.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">I A<i>dork</i> You</a><br />Twitter | <a href="http://twitter.com/aimeereads" rel="nofollow noopener">@aimeereads</a><br />Instagram | <a href="http://instagram.com/aimeereads" rel="nofollow noopener">@aimeereads</a><br />Pinterest | <a href="http://pinterest.com/aimeereads" rel="nofollow noopener">aimeereads</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5275565504205183970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2105738160" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8302173585640695179">this is not a horror story, but it scared the crap out of me. it had me second guessing everything and gave me major trust issues by the end. but i think the unpredictable, and somewhat alarming, nature of this story is quite indicative of how i imagine mental illness can be.<br/><br/>i appreciate how mental illness has garnered more frequent representation and i think the trend needs to continue, if not increase. however, its such a sensitive topic, that if its not handled appropriately or accurately, it</span>
  <span id="freeText8302173585640695179" style="display:none">this is not a horror story, but it scared the crap out of me. it had me second guessing everything and gave me major trust issues by the end. but i think the unpredictable, and somewhat alarming, nature of this story is quite indicative of how i imagine mental illness can be.<br /><br />i appreciate how mental illness has garnered more frequent representation and i think the trend needs to continue, if not increase. however, its such a sensitive topic, that if its not handled appropriately or accurately, it can be quite damaging. i did have some minor issues regarding how treating mental illness is portrayed, as i could see it being a bit problematic for those who do suffer from it. but overall, i thought it was managed fairly well.<br /><br />i also really liked the writing style - its quite strong for being a debut, so that was a lovely surprise. i think there are great things to come from this author and i cant wait to keep a look out for it!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1083401913" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083401913" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1083401913?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22864841-made-you-up">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=autism">autism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2015">best-of-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1083401913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8878879167504576980"><b>I AM SO TOALLY OVERCOME WITH EMOTIONS RIGHT NOW.</b> AGH. How do I even...what do I say?! How?! GAHLKJ FJAKSLDS GHARRRHRH. *ahem* <b>I quite liked this book.</b> It was confusing at times and I guessed many of the plot twists, but somehow I was so totally caught up that the 400-pages just flipped by in a <i>flash</i> and I wanted more, but I also wanted to cry, but I also wanted to rage. So basically YEAH ALL THE EMOTIONS. IT WAS REALLY GOOD. I FEEL LIKE I JUST GOT STABBED IN THE FACE.<br/><br/><b>So it's about schizophrenia,</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8878879167504576980" style="display:none"><b>I AM SO TOALLY OVERCOME WITH EMOTIONS RIGHT NOW.</b> AGH. How do I even...what do I say?! How?! GAHLKJ FJAKSLDS GHARRRHRH. *ahem* <b>I quite liked this book.</b> It was confusing at times and I guessed many of the plot twists, but somehow I was so totally caught up that the 400-pages just flipped by in a <i>flash</i> and I wanted more, but I also wanted to cry, but I also wanted to rage. So basically YEAH ALL THE EMOTIONS. IT WAS REALLY GOOD. I FEEL LIKE I JUST GOT STABBED IN THE FACE.<br /><br /><b>So it's about schizophrenia, but written in a way I've <i>never</i> experienced.</b> I've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18075234.Challenger_Deep" title="Challenger Deep by Neal Shusterman" rel="nofollow noopener">Challenger Deep</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23588512.Alice_and_the_Fly" title="Alice and the Fly by James Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice and the Fly</a>, which both painted the utter confusion of delusions so vividly and were both <i>incredible</i> books to read and I could literally feel what it'd be like to drown in hallucinations. But Made You Up?! IT WAS DIFFERENT. We say Alex as a "normal" person. She said funny things, she had average hopes/dreams, she had normal hobbies, she did chores and held down a job, rode a bike, and took heaps of photos. She was a history nerd. And...she had paranoid schizophrenia. But it wasn't WHO she was. Like I felt <b>there was more to Alex than her mental illness, and I appreciated that 10000%.</b> This book really helped me to understand MORE about schizophrenia and labels and just aGHHHHH SEE THIS IS WHY I LOVE IT SO MUCH?!? I loved Alex. I connected to her, I rooted for her.<br /><br /><b>There's also epic secondary characters that were excellently written and developed.</b> Alex is going to this new school (she got kicked out of her last) and so she meets a motley crew, but notably: Tucker and Miles. DON'T WORRY! THERE'S NO LOVE TRIANGLE. Tucker is a really cool, sweet dude and I liked his easy-going friendship with Alex (YAY FOR PLATONIC FRIENDSHIPS) <br /><br />But Miles?!? <b>Miles is complex.</b> He's German and skinny and a genius and <i>horrible</i> and cruel and unempathetic and has GORGEOUS BLUE EYES and has heart-shattering secrets and afdjsaklda I love Miles. I love him a lot. I do get why he'd be hated by a lot of readers though, but the important thing to realise here is <b>there's a huge chance (though not directly confirmed) that Miles is autistic.</b> So please don't expect him to be neurotypical, because he's not and as an Autistic person, he's SO EXCELLENTLY WRITTEN I COULD CRY. And he's a genius, like he's just a fountain of EXTREME GENIUS. I totally loved his development and the way his and Alex's relationship when from mean pranks to goopy adorable entirely shippable romance. #bestromanceever <br /><br /><blockquote>"I mean that when I'm the one doing everyone else's dirty work, and everyone is afraid of me, I feel safe. I control what happens and to who." (pg. 219)</blockquote><br />(Very Autistic thinking there.)<br /><blockquote>"Heaven knows the boy already seems a little...emotionally stunted. I'm half convinced he's autistic."<br />"So what if he is?"<br />She blinked at me. "What?"<br />"So what if Miles is autistic? And he's not 'emotionally stunted' -- he has emotions like the rest of us. he just has trouble figuring out what they are, sometimes." (pg. 271) </blockquote><br />(FYI Autism IS NOT a mental illness, it's a disability.)<br /><br />I loooooved and so APPRECIATE how this book tackled so many complex topics and treated them WELL and with total respect and impeccable research. Like, just wow and thank you to this author.<br /><br /><b>Unlike other schizophrenic books I've read, this one wasn't hard to follow.</b> Like <i>Challenger Deep</i> totally wrapped my head in a taco and stomped on it -- but Made You Up just read like an average contemporary...with <i>additions</i>. It's also a bit of a "mystery" because there's something WEIRD going on at Alex's new school and she, Tucker, and Miles sort of get to the bottom of it. There's tons of mental illness and disability representation in ALL shapes and sizes. <br /><br />OH OH! And I guessed one of the characters in Alex's life would probably be just a hallucination and OMG I WAS RIGHT ABOUT WHO I GUESSED. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It was so totally her little sister Charlie, because Charlie never interacted with anyone EXCEPT Alex. I actually wondered if Tucker would be at the beginning, but nope, he was real. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>So there were a <i>few</i> things I didn't like.</b> Some of the plot felt a bit..far fetched? I expected a ton of stuff to be "made up" but it wasn't, and, um...yeah?! Like how psycho their principal seemed to be with no one noticing, and the sub-plot around the snake, and how negligent (but loving) Alex's parents were, and how absolutely CRUEL the school was for no reason. And when Alex sneaked out of hospital? Eh, probably not. Also at one point Alex and Miles are returning from A Place I Won't Name and they stop to eat and, despite never eating out nay other time (she's paranoid about poison) Alex eats without an eye blink. Hmm.<br /><br /><b>BUT BASICALLY. ALL OVER? I ABSOLUTELY LOVED THIS MARVELLOUS BOOK.</b> It's so so well written and I will be 1000% done to read anything and everything by this author. And I was actually literally choking on tears (they didn't spill, tho: I am Vulcan) and emotions and just all these super complex feelings. THIS BOOK JUST REALLY KNOTTED INTO MY SOUL AND I'LL NEVER FORGET IT. <br /><br />*** EPIC QUOTES OF AWESOME ***<br /><br /><blockquote> "But - but what if this whole place" -- I had to suck in air again -- "what if everything is inside my head? East Shoal and Scarlet and this bridge and you -- what if your'e not real because nothing is real?"<br />"if nothing's real, then what does it matter?" he said. "You live here. Doesn't that make it real enough?" (pg. 364)<br /><br />"No, you're not a bad person," [Tucker] said. "And Richter isn't a bad person, and I'm not a bad person. We're just people, and people sometimes do stupid things."</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="8878879167504576980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1850938153?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1850938153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5074511934306249114">Ugh. I wanted to like this. Really, I did. But it just...wasn’t in the cards. Or should I say...foretold by the Magic 8-Ball. (That’s a halfhearted reference to this book. Check.)<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/06/06/made-you-up-review/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>God, I’m literally intimidated by the thought of trying to review this. It seems so haaaard to put my thoughts into words. I’ll try. Kind of.<br/> <br/>Let’s start with the good stuff, though. This book focuses on Alex, a high school senior with paranoid schizophrenia. I was <i>hype</i> to read ab</span>
  <span id="freeText5074511934306249114" style="display:none">Ugh. I wanted to like this. Really, I did. But it just...wasn’t in the cards. Or should I say...foretold by the Magic 8-Ball. (That’s a halfhearted reference to this book. Check.)<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/06/06/made-you-up-review/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br /><br />God, I’m literally intimidated by the thought of trying to review this. It seems so haaaard to put my thoughts into words. I’ll try. Kind of.<br /> <br />Let’s start with the good stuff, though. This book focuses on Alex, a high school senior with paranoid schizophrenia. I was <i>hype</i> to read about schizophrenia. I don’t think I’ve ever seen that in YA, and I used to be obsessed with it. (See, schizophrenia doesn’t start presenting itself in most people until the late teenage years, so I used to have a gripping fear that I would have it. But that’s a story for another day. Or never.)<br /> <br />Anyway. I don’t have schizophrenia (or I don’t know I do - shoutout to past me), so I can’t really speak to whether this book is an accurate display of the mental illness. But, to me, an outsider, it <i>felt</i> real. The most popular quote from this book is <i>“Sometimes I think people take reality for granted.”</i>, and I definitely felt like I was questioning reality right alongside Alex. Her hallucinations are often presented as reality, so the reader has to sort out what’s real and what isn’t. If nothing else, it’s an interesting storytelling tactic, and it has some big payoffs.<br /> <br />The only other upside of this book is that there are a few REALLY fun plot twists, and I didn’t see them coming AT ALL. I gasped aloud at one. It’s a ride.<br /> <br />But...everything else about this book <i>filled me with hatred.</i> It was fairly unbearable. We’ll get into it. (I’m appropriating that phrase from straight shooter and podcaster extraordinaire Jon Lovett.)<br /> <br />Whoa, wait, hang on. I just glanced at the synopsis, and this book claims it will “appeal to fans of Wes Anderson, Silver Linings Playbook and Liar.” What in <i>tarnation</i>? Wes ANDERSON? The nerve. What the f*ck this book has to do with that filmmaking genius I may never know. Anyway.<br /> <br />This book is just littered with stupid mistakes and irritating inconsistencies. I didn’t think I was going to review this, so I didn’t write that many down, but I’ll try to dredge some up from my tragic, limited and upsetting memories of this book.<br /> <br />Alex always says her town is small, but it’s made up of like a bajillion “subdivisions” and each “subdivision” is made up of several “neighborhoods.” Also, Alex gives a lot of inconsistent information about finances: her family is “dirt poor,” but they could easily drop $70 for a new school uniform, it’s just that her mom wants to guilt trip her instead. Add to that that her mom is chomping at the bit to ship her off to a mental hospital and we get a whole bunch of confusing info. That shit’s expensive, man. Like, really, really expensive.<br /> <br />On top of that, this book is BONKERS UNREALISTIC. Everything about it. I just wanted to shriek while I was reading it. None of the characters feel real. There’s a psychopathic, cheerleading blonde (clichéd AND unrealistic); a principal who went insane because...he got electrocuted?; a conspiracy in a <i>high school administration</i>; a teenager who “runs jobs” like putting fleas in a kid’s bed and IcyHot in his underwear - and GETS PAID HANDSOMELY BY FELLOW TEENAGERS; a community-service <i>club</i> for troublemakers; an archaeologist father who spends weeks and months in Africa only to make no money...there’s definitely more but I want to repress the memory of this book again. <br /> <br />Alex always complains about how she neverrrr had the chance to have friends - even though she, like, just spent a year attending another school - and suddenly friends just SPRING UP at her new school. Literally spring up. I was like, “Ah, several acquaintances, to whom Alex may perhaps wave in the halls, but certainly not people she could call friends, by any means.” And then suddenly, she’s all, WOWWWW, MY FRIENDSSSS! AMAZING TO HAVE FRIENDS!<br /> <br />And oh, yeah. The love interest in this book? SUCKS. F*ckin’ Miles. He’s the aforementioned job-running teen, and he’s the worsttttt. Apparently, he has problems with empathy, and that’s why he’s okay with doing stuff like LIFE-RUINING PRANKS. It makes no sense, it really doesn’t. There are sociopaths who fit in better than he does. THOUSANDS OF THEM. <br /> <br />But the worst part of this book? I’ve read World War II historical fiction with fewer mentions of Nazis. Everyone calls Miles a Nazi, because he’s Aryan, mean as sh*t, and speaks with a German accent sometimes. After hundreds of pages of this utter bullsh*t, he - one f*cking time - screams that genocide isn’t funny. Already too little, too late, no? Add to that some Nazi sympathizing (he wears a Nazi bomber jacket, and tells Alex that not everyone wanted to be a Nazi) and the fact that he DRESSES LIKE A NAZI FOR PETTY CASH, and I’m f*cking done. It’s not funny. You’re not allowed to try to get me to sympathize with your piece of sh*t asshole of a character by downplaying the systemic murder of millions of people. Seventy years isn’t enough for me to think that’s okay. A THOUSAND years won’t make that okay. And that’s why this shit isn’t getting any bonus points for mental illness rep. Normalization of the Third f*ckin’ Reich deducts as many points as possible.<br /> <br />On top of that, this book is just weirdly written and f*cking annoying, IMO. I was so sick of it by the end I could puke.<br /> <br />Bottom line: There aren’t enough O’s in the world to satisfy my NOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5074511934306249114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1461988787?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

      <a href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
  </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1461988787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17480351668228127945"><br/><i> <b> "Everyone's interesting if you stare at them long enough." </b> </i><br/><br/>I’m peeling off a hangnail from my pinkie as punishment for not having read this sooner. I didn’t even get to vote this for GR 2015 Best YA fiction because I’ve been putting this on hold assuming this was going to be another sad and heavy read about a sick or dying kid because I may have already reached my tolerance limit for these kinds of reads this year. I was wrong about this one. I was so wrong! Now, it’s too late and I’ve got no</span>
  <span id="freeText17480351668228127945" style="display:none"><br><i> <b> "Everyone's interesting if you stare at them long enough." </b> </i><br><br>I’m peeling off a hangnail from my pinkie as punishment for not having read this sooner. I didn’t even get to vote this for GR 2015 Best YA fiction because I’ve been putting this on hold assuming this was going to be another sad and heavy read about a sick or dying kid because I may have already reached my tolerance limit for these kinds of reads this year. I was wrong about this one. I was so wrong! Now, it’s too late and I’ve got nothing left to blame except...ooh wait...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449453293ra/17287416.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, onto the review. I have just recently read a book about the same subject matter: schizophrenia and it was taken rather too heavily. <b>This one was a surprising and refreshing light read although it didn’t take the subject lightly at all.</b> <br><br>In this inventive debut novel, we get to see the meticulous, fascinating and colorful world of someone like Alex, a teenage girl who is schizophrenic. What makes this an invigorating read is that Alex fully knows about her condition and is completely aware that the things she sees may or may not be real. She is such an adorable, admirable character because she doesn’t let her illness stunt or define her. <u>In this story, the reader gets to understand how someone like Alex socially cope and blend in despite her state of mind.</u><br><br>I admire how the story narrated by Alex herself read almost like a fantasy story because of her hilariously creative imagination conjuring out of this world mental pictures like black-clad and armed men on the school’s rooftops or a python slithering stealthily along the school’s ceilings <b>(you’ll never know which is real or not so prepare to be surprised!)</b> The story is made even more ingenious because of this other character, Miles, a boy just as special and as unique, possibly the smartest teenager under the sun but who can’t seem to process emotions properly. <br><br>Put a nerdy schizophrenic girl and an even nerdier boy with mild autism together, add these other sympathetic characters, unexpected plot twist <b>(I was sure one of these important characters weren’t real but OMG! I hadn’t expected it to be that character)</b>, smart and endearing writing, the most unusual romance and mystery with a very satisfying conclusion and you get one of the most incredibly original and adorable YA fiction even written. <br><br>I admit some of the events were a bit far-fetched and some characters and stereotypes a bit overdone but somehow, this charming novel found a special spot in my heart. That spot where unicorns and rainbows and chocolates reside. Except for two or three times when my heart broke, I was grinning like an idiot half of the time. Other times I was giggling and snorting in laughter and the other remaining times, I just wanted to hug the book close to my heart which obviously can be summarized in one sentence. <b> I adore this book! </b> &lt;3 <br><br>For a really wonderful review on the book, you could check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1250995312?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna's.</a>^^</span>
  <a data-text-id="17480351668228127945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1250995312" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1250995312" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1250995312?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-2015-contenders">fave-2015-contenders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-characters">fave-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=romance-i-root-for">romance-i-root-for</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1250995312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15182622058232431151"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432240212i/14911781._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"My throat tightened and my heart swelled painfully in my chest. <i>Please don't let this be a delusion. Please let this be real."</i></b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432240212i/14911782._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>As long as I can remember, I've always been fascinated by schizophrenia, and mental illness, for that matter. Although I've been unable to explain why for years, more that I think about it, more it seems to me that what attracts me so much is <b>the fact that people apprehend and <i>see</i> the world differently, through the lens of their own perception</b>. Perception that they c</span>
  <span id="freeText15182622058232431151" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432240212i/14911781._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"My throat tightened and my heart swelled painfully in my chest. <i>Please don't let this be a delusion. Please let this be real."</i></b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432240212i/14911782._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As long as I can remember, I've always been fascinated by schizophrenia, and mental illness, for that matter. Although I've been unable to explain why for years, more that I think about it, more it seems to me that what attracts me so much is <b>the fact that people apprehend and <i>see</i> the world differently, through the lens of their own perception</b>. Perception that they can never really accept as the reality, because in the end, they know appearances can be fundamentally deceptive. <br><br><b>
  <i>Perception.</i>
</b> What an untrustworthy trick. Indeed in my opinion - all healthy as we are - we don't challenge enough what we see, despite the fact that many experiences show us that we can't trust our eyes more often than not, because our mind overanalyzes everything and shapes what we see to agree with our expectations.<br><br>Anyway, <b>Alex isn't given any choice in the matter : she can't trust herself</b>. She can't trust her own deceitful perception. She can't trust <i>anything</i>, and as followers of the wanderings of her mind, neither can we. <b>Talk about an amazing unreliable narrator</b>. <br> <br>How to live when you can never trust anything you see? How to trust others? How to trust ourselves? Can we, really? <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Was everything made up? Was this whole world inside my head? If I ever woke up from it, would I be inside a padded room somewhere, drooling all over myself?<br>Would I even <i>be</i> myself?"</b>
</blockquote><br><i>Made you Up</i> belongs to my favorite kind of contemporary : <b>those which make you think and question everything, those which purposefully lose you, those which rely more on a psychological level than are action-packed</b>. So, no, don't expect never-ending action. Don't expect astounding settings. But be ready to be captivated from the start, to be hooked. To <b>
  <i>care.</i>
</b> Be ready to eat these words up. As for me, I can't hide that I was delighted by the writing style, because if the sentences can appear to be pretty simple, I often felt suffocated by the feelings oozing from the pages - Despair. Hope. Happiness. Heartbreak. Doubt. So much doubt. <br><br><b>I trusted <i>nothing.</i> I loved <i>everything.</i></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432240212i/14911784._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Truth be told, the characters made me so damn happy, I can't even. Why? <b>Because they're two flawed and unlikeable teenagers, who both have to deal with the wanderings of their minds, their extreme nerdness, and getting to know them was INCREDIBLE</b>.<br><br>The story is told in <b>the refreshing and unique voice of Alex, who's suffered from schizophrenia and paranoia since her early childhood</b>. What she perceives can be tricky, because she always has to keep the possibility of hallucinations in the corner of her head. Therefore she takes pictures and uses them for a reality check. A lot of them. Not to mention the Nazis, the communists, in a word, all these enemies she can't help but see everywhere. What's amazing is the fact that sometimes you forget that Alex suffers from schizophrenia and paranoia and suddenly she thinks stuff like "I'm not going to eat this you know. Because <i>poison</i>" and yes, it takes you by surprise, making you both laugh and cringe (of course that's possible, duh). Although she's rather bitchy more often than not, I loved her because <i>
  <b>1)I am a sucker for both unreliable and flawed characters</b>
</i> and <i>
  <b>2)She always tries to see the better in everyone.</b>
</i> Indeed - and that's so rare! - she <i>questions</i> people's reasons to act the way they do, and where she could have been judgmental, she prefers to give others the benefit of the doubt. <br><br><b>As for Miles, where do I even start?</b> Well, he's a smart-ass asshole. But not the controlling kind. Nope. Sure he's very driven and his inability to always understand people's emotions makes him appear quite the jerk sometimes, but in the end, what do we have? <b>A complex, lonely, heartbreaking boy who needs to protect those he loves</b>, and who rules over a whole hidden world in his head. Hidden world that I was eager to unravel, and - Oh, hell. <b>He maddened me, broke my heart and made me choke on butterflies</b>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Dear Asshole : Thank you for keeping your word and believing me. It was more than I expected. Also, I'm sorry you were inconvenienced by my gluing your locker shut at the beginning of this year. However, I am not sorry that I did it, because it was a lot of fun. <br>Love, Alex."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Moreover, let me tell you that I absolutely adored their interactions and the pranks they set up to each other. Oh, yes, didn't I say that? Miles is the King of pranks. For real. Trust me. Anyway, listening to them was often hilarious and always interesting. I know, I'm such a fangirl right now. <br><br>Finally - <i>drum roll pleaaaaaase</i> - <b>there is no insta-love at all, and no love triangle</b>, but two characters who fall for each other gradually, in a believable way. <br><br>I'm adding here an excerpt from <a href="http://christinareadsya.blogspot.fr/2013/08/lush-on-thursday-with-author-interview.html" rel="nofollow noopener">an interview</a> the author gave and which sums up pretty well what I LOVED in their relationship : <br><br><blockquote>"The last point, about fixing broken people: I have seen a lot--a lot--of YA lit in which one or more characters, usually love interests, believe themselves to be broken or are seen as broken and in need of fixing. That was another thing I was careful with when it came to both Alex and Miles. They don't see themselves as broken, and they don't see each other as broken. There are parts of Alex's world that she genuinely likes, and Miles is well-adapted to working around his emotional and social problems. <b>They don't fix each other, they just understand each other and make things a little easier to bear, like any struggle gets easier when you have someone to share it with"</b>.</blockquote><br>FUCK YEAH.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432240212i/14911785._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To sum up, here's one of the best contemporary YA I read this year, if not the best. Just give these flawed characters a chance, okay? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434546074i/15235264._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="15182622058232431151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1588743339" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1588743339" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1588743339?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1588743339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11169620514512750712">I finished a book after my week long slump that felt like I’d been in for eternity. <br/>THANK YOU, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/43374294-katherine-grace' rel='nofollow noopener'>Katherine</a> for messaging me for a buddy read, otherwise I would’ve been stuck in this rut forever. 😆😘<br/><br/>(I’m going to celebrate by buying a book or six.)<br/><br/>‘Made You Up’ tells the story of a girl who suffers from schizophrenia. Our main character has difficulty differentiating between reality and her hallucinations and in order to cope with that, she takes pictures. <br/><br/>I loved the portrayal of mental health in t</span>
  <span id="freeText11169620514512750712" style="display:none">I finished a book after my week long slump that felt like I’d been in for eternity. <br />THANK YOU, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/43374294-katherine-grace" rel="nofollow noopener">Katherine</a> for messaging me for a buddy read, otherwise I would’ve been stuck in this rut forever. 😆😘<br /><br />(I’m going to celebrate by buying a book or six.)<br /><br />‘Made You Up’ tells the story of a girl who suffers from schizophrenia. Our main character has difficulty differentiating between reality and her hallucinations and in order to cope with that, she takes pictures. <br /><br />I loved the portrayal of mental health in this. It wasn’t the sole focus of the plot; it was more than that (i.e. family, friendship and acceptance) and Alex’s character was pretty awesome. <br /><br />I adored the love interest, Miles. He’s not your typical, will-make-you-swoon-with-six-packs kinda guy. He has his own shit to deal with and I loved how both Alex and Miles came round full circle at the end. They were there for each other and it was beautiful to read. <br /><br />The story didn’t blow me away. I found the plot slightly boring and what kept me reading was the mystery surrounding the characters. Miles was the most complex, but I didn’t find myself getting attached to any of them. I wanted more of an emotional punch to it all. It’s still worth a read, in my opinion. It just wasn’t the most hard-hitting of stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11169620514512750712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
