    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1993729108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1993729108" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1993729108?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of non-toxic mental health narratives</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Elle by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/49148508-may">may ❀</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=author-love">author-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2017">z-faves2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-squads">favorite-squads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=trauma-abuse-recovery">trauma-abuse-recovery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1993729108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7730400757145385437">4 1/2 stars, but I rounded up because... sort of a new favorite. You know how I'm going to review this? <b>Post my old thinkpiece on mental illness tropes in YA, and then proceed to go into how this book smacks it all down</b>. Let's just call this a 5000 word essay on Why Francesca Zappia Is the Only YA Author I Trust With Mental Illness Narrative Framing Anymore. Seriously. <br/><br/><br/>♔ <b> MENTAL ILLNESS IS EXACTLY THIS.</b><br/><br/>You know what trope I hate? The curing trope. You know what trope I'm tired of? The everything</span>
  <span id="freeText7730400757145385437" style="display:none">4 1/2 stars, but I rounded up because... sort of a new favorite. You know how I'm going to review this? <b>Post my old thinkpiece on mental illness tropes in YA, and then proceed to go into how this book smacks it all down</b>. Let's just call this a 5000 word essay on Why Francesca Zappia Is the Only YA Author I Trust With Mental Illness Narrative Framing Anymore. Seriously. <br /><br /><br />♔ <b> MENTAL ILLNESS IS EXACTLY THIS.</b><br /><br />You know what trope I hate? The curing trope. You know what trope I'm tired of? The everything's-fine-until-I-go-off-meds trope. This book smacks both of those tropes down into the abyss. <b>Alex is <i>not</i> cured.</b> She starts the book with schizophrenia, and she ends the book with schizophrenia. <br /><br />You know what else I loved? <b>The acknowledgement of Alex's agency</b>. So many books about mentally ill people take away all their agency, turning the book into a parents-are-always-right extravaganza that feels disrespectful to mentally ill people themselves, especially those who are victims of parental abuse. <b>I love that this book treats Alex like a fucking human being</b>. I love that she's a reasonable person who <i>happens</i> to sometimes be unsure of what's real and not real. <br /><br />You know what makes me want to cry? The fact that <b>y'all cannot get the balance right between mental-illness-makes-you-quirky and mental-illness-makes-you-evil</b>. And yet <b>Zappia gets it so right.</b> Alex and Miles are so <i>human</i>. They're not some goddamn props for a thinly veiled romance that's supposed to be more emo because mental illness!! real problems!! but really just feels disrespectful and gross. But they're also not these especially evil people. They feel like human fucking beings and I <i>love</i> that. Seriously, I love it and I have so much respect for Zappia for handling this well. <br /><br />Obviously, I can't speak for the representation of schizophrenia being <i>accurate</i>. But I can definitely guarantee that it's empathetic. I would feel comfortable recommending this to any mentally ill person, and that's more than I can say for a lot of the books in this genre. <br /><br /><br />♔ <b>THE BOOK ITSELF ROCKS</b> <br /><br />Aside from mental health handling, this is really just a fantastic book. First of all, the <b>character work</b> is fabulous. Alex is one of the greatest characters ever. She's <i>so</i> strong. I love that she's so aware of herself and constantly questioning what's real and what's fake. I love that she's not your typical written-by-gross-tropes mentally ill protagonist. I just love her. <br /><br /><b>And I loved the romance!!</b> Miles, too, is a fantastically developed character. He's so weirdly dorky and offbeat. But he's also not the fake-quirky love interest you see in mental illness books sometimes. <br /><br />Zappia's <b>plotting</b> is also quite well-handled. <i>Made You Up</i> is fairly exciting and <b>twisty</b> for a typical contemporary book. I really didn't expect many of the twists - a few didn't even pop into my mind as possibilities. <br /><br /><br />♔ <b>THE ENDING FALLS..........</b><br />flat. <br /><br /><b>I did have mixed feelings on the ending</b>. I don't think it's terrible - I just feel <b>it's not built up well</b>. Spoilers ahead, by the way. Alex checks herself into a mental health facility. Now this isn't a bad ending - I actually think it's a good thing for her future. I just don't think this is built up well. Because the book portraying the mental health center as bad the whole way through - Alex's mindset - and then switching at the last minute - the real truth - Alex's final decision feels quite false and almost like a bad thing. I also think we don't get the sense that Alex is getting worse until the very end. She has some quote about “not being able to tell anymore” but she hasn't been able to tell in <i>years</i>. It felt a bit half-assed.<br /><br />I like that the narrative emphasizes how this was her choice, something <i>she</i> did to combat her own issues. <b>Yay for emphasis on the agency of mentally ill people!!</b> What I didn't like was the implication of “her mom was right all along.” Yes, her mom was right about her mental illness. Her mom was <i>not</i> right about forcing her into an psychiatric hospital. Whether that was a good decision or not, it felt to me that her mother was trying to control her, not help her get better. <br /><br />Part of this is coming from my heavy dislike for Alex's mom; hence my dissatisfaction with how ending treats her character. <b>Alex's mom is a trash person, and the book knows this</b>. I love that the book knows this. Unfortunately, <b>I don't think the book was willing to stick with it.</b> I think Zappia didn't want to ruffle feathers, so she decided to go with “she had Alex's best intentions at heart.” Here's the thing: I don't think she did. And even if she did, I don't think it justifies her actions. I think she's an <b>abusive parent</b> looking for control. and I really wish Alex had gotten to tell her off more at the end as well. <br /><br />But I honestly love this book with so much of my heart that I really want to just give it a five. It's just too good. <br /><br />This was a BR with Romie, and again, I am SO SORRY for reading these last 170 pages without you. It was so great. <br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/kaz_inej" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7730400757145385437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1697143195" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1697143195" />
    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26402455-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560612398p2/26402455.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_1767749996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1767749996" />
    <a title="Tweebs♥️ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35431290-tweebs"><img alt="Tweebs♥️ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600454813p2/35431290.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1767749996?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tweebs♥️ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tweebs♥️ " href="/user/show/35431290-tweebs">Tweebs♥️ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35431290-tweebs?shelf=books-that-killed-me-and-my-ghost">books-that-killed-me-and-my-ghost</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1767749996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7461210575637898266"><i>“Everyone's interesting if you stare at them long enough.”</i><br/><br/><b>*snort*</b><br/><br/>Well, I’ll be damned. If I stare at this book any longer, I think I will throw it across the Atlantic Ocean for making me into this…...<i>emotional hot mess.</i> Speaking, of hot mess, I’m pretty sure this review will be one so, buckle up kids. <br/><br/><b>YOU ARE IN FOR A RIDE!! </b><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477846966ra/21000312.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>This book was quite a surprise. I<b> DID NOT </b> expect to have my bum bum blown away by the awesomeness. I dived into this book thinking it was going to be cute and cliche. Like </span>
  <span id="freeText7461210575637898266" style="display:none"><i>“Everyone's interesting if you stare at them long enough.”</i><br><br><b>*snort*</b><br><br>Well, I’ll be damned. If I stare at this book any longer, I think I will throw it across the Atlantic Ocean for making me into this…...<i>emotional hot mess.</i> Speaking, of hot mess, I’m pretty sure this review will be one so, buckle up kids. <br><br><b>YOU ARE IN FOR A RIDE!! </b><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477846966ra/21000312.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>This book was quite a surprise. I<b> DID NOT </b> expect to have my bum bum blown away by the awesomeness. I dived into this book thinking it was going to be cute and cliche. Like those typical reads where you think you already know everything that's going to happen. <br><br>I assure you, <b>THAT IS NOT WHAT YOU GET FROM THIS BOOK…...AT ALL</b>. Okay, I lied. Maybe, cute. Yes, you’ll definitely get some cute. The thing you'll mostly find in here is pain, suffering, and a lot of questioning oneself. <br><br><b>
  <i>“I didn't have the luxury of taking reality for granted. And I wouldn't say I hated people who did, because that's just about everyone. I didn't hate them. They didn't live in my world. <br><br>But that never stopped me from wishing I lived in theirs.” </i>
</b><br><br><br>Don't worry, it's not entirely based to make you cry but it'll make you laugh as well ;) <br><br><br>I’m just so happy that I gave this book a chance because I’d be missing out. Plus, you’d be missing out if I missed out because who else is going to convince you guys to read this?????? Just who????? <br><br>I adored this book for many things. One of them being the portrayal of mental illness. I've never read a book with the main character suffering from schizophrenia. It was really refreshing. I loved how the author didn't feel the need to revolve the plot entirely on the subject of schizophrenia. It was the focus but it wasn't <b>THE</b> focus. <i>Get it??????</i> <br><br>Alex, the main character had difficulties differentiating between reality and imagination. She would take pictures on her camera in hopes that it wasn't a hallucination. She questions her entire life majority of the time and <b>YES IT AFFECTED ME.</b> I legit questioned my life along with her. <br><br><i>
  <b>“I am real. This”–he put his other hand over the first-“is real. You see me interacting with other people all day long, don’t you? I talk to people; I affect things in the world. I cause things to happen. I am real.”<br>“But-but what if this whole place”-I had to suck in air again-“what if everything is inside my head? East Shoal and Scarlet and this bridge and you-what if you’re not real because nothing is real?”<br>“If nothing’s real, then what does it matter?” he said. “You live here. Doesn’t that make it real enough?” </b>
</i><br><br><br>The thing I loved about the author is that she approached the subject of schizophrenia in a sort of humorous way. Alex, was full of sass, funny, quirky and yes WEIRD but it made me cherish her character even more. She wasn't one of those typical bland type of characters which have no flavor in their personalities. Or basically, the author forgets the fact that maybe people with mental illness <b> CAN </b> have a personality. Francesca Zappia added some seasoning to spice up Alex's personality and <b>DAMN WAS IT A PERSONALITY!! </b><br><br>For real, the author seriously added a lot of seasoning to Alex's personality like :<br><br><b>
  <i>“Dear Asshole: Thank you for keeping your word and believing me. It was more than I expected. Also, I'm sorry you were inconvenienced by my gluing your locker shut at the beginning of this year. However, I am not sorry that I did it, because it was a lot of fun. Love, Alex.” <br><br>AND<br><br>“Was there some kind of law about drop-kicking assholes in the face? Probably. They always had laws against things that needed to be done.” </i>
</b><br><br><br>Miles, is not one of those typical love interests where they come in and save the day. <b>NOPEEEEEEE. </b> You can scratch that off your list. He is just as sassy as she is. No seriously like omfg. At first, you get the sense of <b>"Wtf is wrong with him??" </b> then he obviously grows on you as you progress through the story. Damn, did he grow on <b>ME.</b> I just love him. End of story. No words. On the other hand, the romance was just....<b>AWWWWWW</b>. That's all I have to say. Just <b>AWWWWWWWWW. </b><br><br>Wow, the plot, the characters, and the romance were spot on. It was written very well and it's easy to follow. <b>BASICALLY, </b>this is a must read for anyone who doesn't know anything about schizophrenia and anyone with schizophrenia !! You'll love it. I can bet money on that ;) <br><br><b>OHHHHH</b> I can't forget to mention the very thing that CAUGHT my attention about this book. <br><br><b>*drum roll* </b><br><br>This <b>COVER.</b>. <i>Boyyyyyyy</i>, I was simply mesmerized by the beauty. I lowkey picked this book up because of THAT COVER. It’s utterly <b>BOOTIFUL. </b><br><br><b>B<br>O<br>O<br>T<br>I<br>F<br>U<br>L</b><br><br>I just want to state the fact that y'all are about to have the biggest mind fuck towards the end. Trust me, it's left better unsaid. You'll definitely come out of it like:<br><br><b>"WAS THIS SHIT REAL OR NAHHHHH???" </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7461210575637898266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1286318367" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1286318367" />
    <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna"><img alt="✦❋Arianna✦❋" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420671997p2/23370948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1286318367?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✦❋Arianna✦❋" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna">✦❋Arianna✦❋</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1286318367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2209916308006872485"><b>
  <u>4 Stars!!</u>
</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Reality is merely an illusion, albeit a very persistent one” – Albert Einstein</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432906725i/15019488.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>For some reason I’m always reluctant to start a YA novel and I’m always reluctant to start a book with this subject matter – mental illness. And no, not because I don’t enjoy them. In fact, I’ve always been fascinated by books about mental health. To be honest <i>“Made You Up”</i> was very different from what I expected. It’s a compelling, moving, refreshing story about a girl who lives in her own wo</span>
  <span id="freeText2209916308006872485" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>4 Stars!!</u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Reality is merely an illusion, albeit a very persistent one” – Albert Einstein</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432906725i/15019488.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For some reason I’m always reluctant to start a YA novel and I’m always reluctant to start a book with this subject matter – mental illness. And no, not because I don’t enjoy them. In fact, I’ve always been fascinated by books about mental health. To be honest <i>“Made You Up”</i> was very different from what I expected. It’s a compelling, moving, refreshing story about a girl who lives in her own world, a world between reality and hallucination. It’s a story that deals not only with mental illness, but family drama as well. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Sometimes I think people take reality for granted.<br><br>I mean like how you can tell the difference between a dream and real life. When you’re in the dream you may not know it, but as soon as you wake up, you know that your dream was a dream and whatever happened in it, good or bad, wasn’t real.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>When she was seven years old, Alex, helped by a boy, freed all the lobsters in a supermarket. The boy, a beautiful boy, with blue eyes who smelled like fish agreed to be her friend. But suddenly he disappeared. Was the boy real? Nobody saw him, so maybe her mind made him up. <br><br>Alex was diagnosed with schizophrenia at thirteen and with paranoia a year later. Her medication helped her sometimes and she knew that when the world was not as colorful and interesting as it normally was. Years later, Alex is starting her senior year of high school. She still struggles with this mental illness who affects her daily life. She performs a perimeter check wherever she goes, she searches for poison in the food her mother wants her to eat, she’s terrified by Nazis, she’s convinced the communists are coming for her and she takes photographs of everything around her to help her distinguish between reality and her hallucinations. Yes, Alex is really messed up.<br><br>She wants to be 'normal'. She wants to try to be 'normal'. She wants to prove that she can be 'normal' even if every day everything can get confusing. She wants to go to college, to have friends and maybe to have a boyfriend, she wants to have a life. She wants to live, not only exist. She works at Finnegan’s Restaurant and all she wants is to fit at her new high school. She has fears like everyone else, the biggest – someone to discover about her illness. At her new high school she makes friends, she meets Miles, a boy with blue eyes who might be the boy who helped her free the lobsters many years ago, she discovers what means to be truly accepted. <br><br>The story is told entirely from Alex’s perspective, so you will question everything since she’s an unreliable character. What is real and what is just a hallucination? I must admit this fact was a little frustrating at times, yet fascinating. <br><br>The main characters is this book are endearing, unique and very vivid. And most important they will make you feel. Alex was a complex, endearing character from the start. She has flaws and obviously insecurities, she felt 100% real and she’s even relatable. Yes, I related with her. No, not because I suffer from schizophrenia, but because like Alex I want to be accepted. Every one of us wants that, right? She’s smart and witty and brave as well. Her determination and courage are absolutely admirable. Mrs. Zappia did a great job portraying her character who has many layers. We get to see her at school and at home, with her parents, with her sister, with her friends, with her enemies and with Miles. I loved the fact she’s full of hope and the fact that she actually knows that she’s different. She was very mature most of the time and I loved how responsible she was. There were moments when my heart broke for her and when I just wanted to give her a hug. <br><br>Miles, like Alex is a unique character as well. He also has his own flaws. He’s very smart. Actually he’s a genius. He’s very defensive, arrogant, a real smart-ass and he can really be an a**hole. Even with Alex. He can be cruel and everyone is terrified of him for a certain reason. He also does odd jobs for money. Miles is a relatable character as well and he’s well developed. As the story progressed you will get to know him better, to sympathize with him and ultimately fall for him. Personally I did. Miles’s story was heartbreaking. Like Alex, he’s not ‘normal’. He has some emotional problems. He wants to seem tough, but actually he’s just as lost as Alex. He’s lonely, but Alex will show him that he’s not alone. While at first he’s a prick, later he’s portrayed as a sweet, attentive and thoughtful boy who truly cares for Alex, who wants to help her in any way he can, who understands and supports her like no other. Needless to say I REALLY liked Miles.<br> <br>From the moment I read the prologue I knew it will be a good read. I love it! It was captivating, powerful and very important for what will come next.<br> <br>The romance wasn’t the main focus of the story. And I liked it! However, their romance was adorable and unique. They are perfect for each other in a strange kind of way and I loved the honesty between them and the fact they give each other what they really need – ACCEPTANCE. <br><br>Alex’s relationship with her parents felt real. I didn’t agree with their decisions all the time and some of their attitudes toward some aspects frustrated me like hell. However, I knew they love Alex and want what’s best for her. I also felt for them. It must be terrifying to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[lose a child <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and to have another one who suffers from schizophrenia, to know you can’t do anything about it, to see him struggle everyday with such a cruel reality. <br><br>The secondary characters were interesting and most of them endearing as well. I liked how all of them interacted with each other, but what I loved the most is Alex and Miles's interactions. There’s no insta-love here. They start from some sort of enemies, they slowly become friends and eventually something more. They felt good together. I really felt they complete each other and I loved all their moments together. <br><br>This novel has it all. It has some sweet moments, some funny moments and also gut wrenching moments. It also has some mystery. Personally I didn’t care about this aspect of the story. I don’t know why exactly, but well...I didn’t. Anyway, even this aspect is done well. The author did a wonderful job portraying a character who suffers from paranoia and schizophrenia ans she did it in a caring, respectful way. <br><br>IMO, the story dragged a little in the first half. I wasn’t bored, but I wanted something to happen...something more exiting I guess. Anyway, in the end I was happy with what I’ve got. <br><br>All in all, <i>“Made You Up”</i> was a fascinating, powerful read with unique characters, interesting storyline and engaging writing. This was my first read by this author (since this was a debut, btw a great debut, one of the best I’ve read) and I’m sure it won’t be my last. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"My throat tightened and my heart swelled painfully in my chest.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>
      <u>Please don't let this be a delusion. Please let this be real."</u>
    </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432906725ra/15019489.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2209916308006872485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1494733238?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-ya-challenge">2018-ya-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-audio">2018-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-four-stars">2018-four-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1494733238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1234219476604891898"><b>4 stars!!!</b> <br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%2011/IMG_1933_zpsnmgayn9u.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536331809i/26267533._SY540_.png' alt=' photo IMG_1933_zpsnmgayn9u.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>Made You Up</i> is a unique and riveting tale of a teenage girl named Alex. Alex is a teenager who is living with mental illness. She has schizophrenia and has trouble knowing what is real and what isn’t sometimes. I cannot imagine being in Alex’s shoes. The story was fascinating but equally terrifying knowing that people are dealing with this very serious disorder. <br/><br/>I loved Alex’s character. I thought she was fierce and honestly was trying to live her very best life, as difficult as i</span>
  <span id="freeText1234219476604891898" style="display:none"><b>4 stars!!!</b> <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%2011/IMG_1933_zpsnmgayn9u.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536331809i/26267533._SY540_.png" alt=" photo IMG_1933_zpsnmgayn9u.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Made You Up</i> is a unique and riveting tale of a teenage girl named Alex. Alex is a teenager who is living with mental illness. She has schizophrenia and has trouble knowing what is real and what isn’t sometimes. I cannot imagine being in Alex’s shoes. The story was fascinating but equally terrifying knowing that people are dealing with this very serious disorder. <br><br>I loved Alex’s character. I thought she was fierce and honestly was trying to live her very best life, as difficult as it could be. She was a good person. And then there was Miles. I loved the little enemies to friends relationship they had. I loved that Miles accepted her for who she was. His life was difficult in a different way, and even though at first I wasn’t sure about him, I adored him by the end of the book. I shipped these two so hard, and even though a relationship for Alex seemed impossible at times, I hoped they could be together. <br><br>This is one of those books that really, truly made me think and feel. As a nurse, I’ve dealt with a lot of people with mental health issues, but none as serious as this at such a young age. I think the author handled the topic very well, and the book was interesting, informative, and entertaining. I’m looking forward to reading more by this author. I enjoyed this one a lot.</span>

<div id="review_1082438355" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1082438355" />
    <a title="Paula M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23287093-paula-m"><img alt="Paula M" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601006204p2/23287093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1082438355?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula M" href="/user/show/23287093-paula-m">Paula M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22864841-made-you-up">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23287093-paula-m?shelf=all-them-feels">all-them-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23287093-paula-m?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23287093-paula-m?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23287093-paula-m?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1082438355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9739296071448060061"><blockquote>
  <br/>
   
    <strong>"Are you real?"</strong>
   
  <br/>
</blockquote><br/> 
  <a href='http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-fzyOlGb0tAQ/VQSIETtK2lI/AAAAAAAAJTo/cUo-zSu89j4/s280/giphy%2B(4).gif' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433220443ra/15066841.gif' alt='Paula' width='400' height='200' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
 <br/> Right after reading this book, my feelings was all over the place. And if you don't know, when a book does that to you it only means one thing: the book is all kinds of amazing. <strong>Made You Up is such a powerful and poignant novel. It was engrossing to the point that the book is absolutely gripped inside your heart and the desire to let go... is nonexistent.</strong><br/><br/> I love how unreliable our main character is. <strong>I'm the kind of reader who always puts herself </strong></span>
  <span id="freeText9739296071448060061" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <br>
   
    <strong>"Are you real?"</strong>
   
  <br>
</blockquote><br> 
  <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-fzyOlGb0tAQ/VQSIETtK2lI/AAAAAAAAJTo/cUo-zSu89j4/s280/giphy%2B(4).gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433220443ra/15066841.gif" alt="Paula" width="400" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
 <br> Right after reading this book, my feelings was all over the place. And if you don't know, when a book does that to you it only means one thing: the book is all kinds of amazing. <strong>Made You Up is such a powerful and poignant novel. It was engrossing to the point that the book is absolutely gripped inside your heart and the desire to let go... is nonexistent.</strong><br><br> I love how unreliable our main character is. <strong>I'm the kind of reader who always puts herself in the main character's shoes so that I can truly experience the whole novel.</strong> And I would be lying if I say that doing that is such a challenge when you're reading MADE YOU UP. Is it real? Or is it not? <strong>Fear is gnawing inside of me throughout the novel because there's a possibility that a certain character or a certain event that happened may not be real.</strong> And I can't have that because every character in this story is attached to me from the moment Francesca introduced them to me. They are real. At least to me.<br><br> <strong>Don't you just love books that challenges you? That makes you think? That makes you understand another human being that you have different opinion about before? Don't you just love books that makes you understand?</strong> There may be a lot of books with schizophrenic as a main character but only a few can make you sympathize or make you fully feel how that main character feels. Francesca just did all that and I am blown away.<br><br> There's a certain boy that I fell for and I don't know how to move on from him. Miles. <strong>How do I explain Miles to people?</strong> Miles is the 70% of reasons why I adore Francesca. There, I said it. Alex is phenomenal as a heroine and I absolutely admired Jetta and the crew, even Celia was dear to me. But Miles, <em>Miles is golden.</em> Not just because he makes me swoon or that he's hated by everyone or that he has that accent that everybody is making fun of... its because Miles is layered. <strong>He's the kind of guy you WANT to get to know slowly and deeply.</strong> Its not because of his baggage or his jerky exterior but because he is Miles. And that's enough reason.<br><br> <strong>Made You Up is absolutely, without a doubt, one of the best book I've read this year.</strong> It's gripping. It's emotional. It's real. <strong>A brilliant writing plus thought provoking plot and terrific characters, Francesca just made a recipe for a successful novel that is perfect for every person who can read.</strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="9739296071448060061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1096031460" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1096031460" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1096031460?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=r2r-complete">r2r-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=mental-health-problem">mental-health-problem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1096031460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4970487778795153145">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to HarperCollins and Edelweiss.)<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“My first-ever friend was a hallucination: a sparkling entry on my new resume as a crazy person.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432669210i/14996727._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was a quirky story about a girl suffering from schizophrenia, and her doubts over what was real, and what was a hallucination.<br/><br/>Alex was a sweet girl, and I felt quite sorry for her and what she was going through; being diagnosed with schizophrenia at such a young age, bei</span>
  <span id="freeText4970487778795153145" style="display:none">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to HarperCollins and Edelweiss.)<br><br><b>
  <i>“My first-ever friend was a hallucination: a sparkling entry on my new resume as a crazy person.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432669210i/14996727._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was a quirky story about a girl suffering from schizophrenia, and her doubts over what was real, and what was a hallucination.<br><br>Alex was a sweet girl, and I felt quite sorry for her and what she was going through; being diagnosed with schizophrenia at such a young age, being unable to know what was really happening and what she was hallucinating, and the bullying she went through from other kids was just a lot for her to deal with. I found Miles to be a bit of an odd character, but he seemed to be good for Alex, which was important as she needed someone to support her.<br><br><i>
  <b>“I didn’t hate them. They didn’t live in my world.<br>But that never stopped me from wishing I lived in theirs.”</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432669210i/14996728._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline in this was about Alex starting at a new school, meeting Miles, and getting up to some mischief, and we also got a few twists thrown in when we would discover that something was in fact a hallucination rather than really happening to poor Alex!<br>We did get a bit of romance, but it didn’t really appeal to me all that much.<br><br><b>
  <i>“That is Miles Richter,” I said to Lil. “And he is not imaginary, thank you very much.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394654254i/8883109.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending to this was pretty good, but my favourite part of the story was definitely the twists we got thrown at the end!<br>7 out of 10</span>
  <a data-text-id="4970487778795153145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1756121909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1756121909" />
    <a title="⊱ Poppy ⊰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47555322-poppy"><img alt="⊱ Poppy ⊰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475924055p2/47555322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1756121909?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="⊱ Poppy ⊰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="⊱ Poppy ⊰" href="/user/show/47555322-poppy">⊱ Poppy ⊰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47555322-poppy?shelf=hyped-books">hyped-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47555322-poppy?shelf=cover-porn">cover-porn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47555322-poppy?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47555322-poppy?shelf=romance-comedy">romance-comedy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47555322-poppy?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47555322-poppy?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47555322-poppy?shelf=so-many-feels">so-many-feels</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756121909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1136848921906063383"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What you loved as a child, you will love forever.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473932736i/20532045._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Wow, I am shocked, i really didn't expect that it would be this good.</i><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17661416.Made_You_Up' title='Made You Up by Francesca Zappia' rel='nofollow noopener'>Made You Up</a> is a book, <b>that will make you question everything you know.</b> It griped me from the very first page. I was real wary to read it, because Mental Illness book doesn't dwell well with me, because Literally in every book the illness is dragged, and i know it because its my it my field of expertise, we literally work hard to know and treat these patients and fo</span>
  <span id="freeText1136848921906063383" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What you loved as a child, you will love forever.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473932736i/20532045._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Wow, I am shocked, i really didn't expect that it would be this good.</i><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17661416.Made_You_Up" title="Made You Up by Francesca Zappia" rel="nofollow noopener">Made You Up</a> is a book, <b>that will make you question everything you know.</b> It griped me from the very first page. I was real wary to read it, because Mental Illness book doesn't dwell well with me, because Literally in every book the illness is dragged, and i know it because its my it my field of expertise, we literally work hard to know and treat these patients and for me it's literally eye rolling scene whenever they dragged a illness and treat it wrong. <br><br>That's why I am really picky when it comes to Mental Illness books, I am not saying this book was perfect in the "Mental Illness" Department but it was good if compared to other books of this kind. Surely there was a little bit dragging out at some points but that is reasonable because nothing is perfect. and the second reason of may wariness was the <b>title</b>, <i>"Made You Up"</i> <u>for me its like the title is speaking that you will read it and believe it and then i will make it all go, on the very last page.</u> and <b>Believe me i was waiting for the shoe to be dropped till the last fucking page, it was like i am reading a thriller not a contemporary.</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Dear Asshole: <br>Thank you for keeping your word and believing me. It was more than I expected. Also, I'm sorry you were inconvenienced by my gluing your locker shut at the beginning of this year. However, I am not sorry that I did it, because it was a lot of fun.<br>Love, Alex.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473932736i/20532046._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17661416.Made_You_Up" title="Made You Up by Francesca Zappia" rel="nofollow noopener">Made You Up</a> is book, full of <i>Love, friendship, hardships, highschool bullies, bitches, detentions, first love, paranoia, mental illness, suspense that will kill you till the very last page, family hardships and LIFE.</i><br><br><b>Alex</b> well truth to be told when it comes to female MC's i really am not a big fan of female characters and only some of them made a place in my heart and Alex was one of them, <b>a twisted teenager with Schizophrenia, who can't tell what's the difference between real and hallucinations.</b> what she was dealing with was really difficult to comprehend because <i>how can we live when out of nowhere the thing became a hallucination when al of your life you think that it was real??</i> Alex was a victim of paranoia from her childhood she don't do anything without a perimeter check and don't even eat anything because it might had anykind of poison, <i>she don't even touch anyone or let them touch her.</i> I loved her strength yeah for me she was brave, because who would have strength to live a normal life where everyone thinks you are crazy?? I am sucker for twisted characters and she was one of the most twisted persons. I loved her sense of humour. The girl had a really good spirits even the world of her was crumbling form its axis. <br><br><b>Miles</b>, well if i start explaining miles it would be a sort of rambling from a fangirl not a review so for miles i would just highlight some points or you'll be the victim of <i>poppy's fangirl episode.</i><br><i>♥ He is the MOST heart-breaking soft and loving <b>Asshole</b>, I've ever read.<br>♥ He is a jerk who plays pranks on everyone for money because of the most emotional reason yo'll ever find<br>♥ He protects everyone is loves. Even if it cause him to do anything.<br>♥ He loves Alex.<br>♥ He was complex, Intriguing, heartbroken, and a confuse personalty with a witty sense humour.<br>♥ I loved his "Quirked one eyebrow raised" expression . <i>ahh the butterflies!</i><br>♥ and he is <b>MILES</b> what not to love about him. and<br>♥ He has Alexithymia- a mental illness in which you can't comprehend your or anyone's emotions.<br>♥ And yet he was always there when anyone needs him, when alex need him.<br>♥ THE END ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥</i><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i><b>“I am real. This”</b>–he put his other hand over the first-<b>“is real. You see me interacting with other people all day long, don’t you? I talk to people; I affect things in the world. I cause things to happen. I am real.”</b><br><br><b>“But-but what if this whole place”</b>-I had to suck in air again-<b>“what if everything is inside my head? East Shoal and Scarlet and this bridge and you-what if you’re not real because nothing is real?”</b><br><br><b>“If nothing’s real, then what does it matter?”</b> he said. <b>“You live here. Doesn’t that make it real enough?”</b></i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473932736i/20532047._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Alex &amp; Miles</b> was together was everything you'll ever need, i loved the interaction and their little pranks that they put on eachother and and and their 3 turn 20 ask me something question game were hilarious, these two history junkies know almost everything and i loved them. There was so many moments that i laugh out loud on their pranks and interactions they never did make me bore or roll my eyes on them. They both were crushed but whole with eachother. <b>I just adored them so much!!</b><br><br>Did i tell you that other than Alex and Miles, i almost loved EVERYONE in this book, <b>even the bitch celia and the psycho McCoy</b>, this book was packed with suspense and will make you glued to your seat till the very last page, i was shocked to learn how this book can deal with the mental illness with a really suspenseful plot at the very same time. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7009633.Francesca_Zappia" title="Francesca Zappia" rel="nofollow noopener">Francesca Zappia</a> i must say <b>you really made a fine piece of work with this book, literally outstanding.</b> I was rooting for the MC's from the very first page. this was the mother of <b>SLOW BURN ROMANCE</b> but it won't bore you to death with it, i swear! :P <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“No, you're not a bad person," he said.<br>"And Richter isn't a bad person, and I'm not a bad person. We're just people, and people sometimes do stupid things.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430194201i/14690928._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well you must be thinking that if i loved this book so much why i didn't give it 5 Stars well because there are still something that we didn't get the answers clearly and that made me a little bit of wary and i wanted a Epilogue which was not there. But overall i really loved this book. So, <b>Read it guys, what are you waiting for, i mean LITERALLY YOU HAVE TO READ THIS ASAP!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1136848921906063383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1175749617" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1175749617" />
    <a title="Cee (The Mistress Case)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37784247-cee-the-mistress-case"><img alt="Cee (The Mistress Case)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475961354p2/37784247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1175749617?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cee (The Mistress Case)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cee (The Mistress Case)" href="/user/show/37784247-cee-the-mistress-case">Cee (The Mistress Case)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37784247-cee-the-mistress-case?shelf=waving-at-you-in-my-rearview-mirror">waving-at-you-in-my-rearview-mirror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37784247-cee-the-mistress-case?shelf=the-hype-failed-me">the-hype-failed-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37784247-cee-the-mistress-case?shelf=u-made-society-hang-itself">u-made-society-hang-itself</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1175749617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4076905755623390854"><u>How I know my Magic 8 Ball is reliable</u><br/><br/><br/>*Before Reading*<br/><br/><b>Cee:</b> Magic 8 Ball, will <i>Made You Up</i> try to kill me?<br/><br/><b>Magic 8 Ball:</b> Concentrate and ask again.<br/><br/><b>Cee:</b> You know? The kind where a book sucks the soul out of you, drop by drop, until you're on the floor rolling around in your own filth because you both love and hate yourself for picking up this book in the first place?<br/><br/><b>Magic 8 Ball:</b> Reply hazy. Try again later.<br/><br/><b>Cee:</b> Can you at least tell me if I'll like it or not?<br/><br/><b>Magic 8 Ball:</b> Outlook not so good.<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>*Afte</span>
  <span id="freeText4076905755623390854" style="display:none"><u>How I know my Magic 8 Ball is reliable</u><br /><br /><br />*Before Reading*<br /><br /><b>Cee:</b> Magic 8 Ball, will <i>Made You Up</i> try to kill me?<br /><br /><b>Magic 8 Ball:</b> Concentrate and ask again.<br /><br /><b>Cee:</b> You know? The kind where a book sucks the soul out of you, drop by drop, until you're on the floor rolling around in your own filth because you both love and hate yourself for picking up this book in the first place?<br /><br /><b>Magic 8 Ball:</b> Reply hazy. Try again later.<br /><br /><b>Cee:</b> Can you at least tell me if I'll like it or not?<br /><br /><b>Magic 8 Ball:</b> Outlook not so good.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />*After Reading* *will contain spoilers*<br /><br /><b>Cee:</b> Do I think this book is cute?<br /><br /><b>Magic 8 Ball:</b> My reply is no.<br /><br /><b>Cee:</b> Do I think this book is angsty?<br /><br /><b>Magic 8 Ball:</b> My sources say no.<br /><br /><b>Cee:</b> Do you know why?<br /><br /><b>Magic 8 Ball:</b> Don't count on it.<br /><br /><b>Cee:</b> This is one of those times when a WRITER SHOULD WRITE WHAT THEY KNOW. If you plan to read <i>Made You Up</i>, do your research first so you aren't force-fed lies because anyone these days can slap mental illness onto the pages of a romance novel. <i>Made You Up</i> did not give me insight into schizophrenia. It made schizophrenia look like a pretentious illness with a stick up its ass. And believe me, saying this makes me feel like the asshole here. I don't claim to know jack squat about schizophrenia, but it doesn't take a genius to figure out that Alex didn't fit the bill. Let's give credit where credit is due— Francesca Zappia sure knows how to be crafty with mental illness because if I could create my own symptoms and get a kick out of making a book "fun," I probably would. Then I would cross my fingers and hope all of my readers swoon over my quirky and oh-so-intelligent characters. Yayy!<br /><br />And as if the misrepresentation of mental illness, the boring characters, and the absentminded plot weren't enough to irked me, there was Charlie. I smelled that bullshit from hundreds of pages away and when shit hit the fan, I had to roll my eyes and skimmed the drama. She was a cheap tool to create angst. She really fucking was.<br /><br />So there you have it. I had high expectations for <i>Made You Up.</i> I wanted it to challenge me on many levels from intellectual to emotional to morally, but the book fell flat and was too predictable and fake for me to give a rat's ass about it. It was like somebody trolled on my nonexistent feels.<br /><br />In closing, my Magic 8 Ball is smarter than this book. Don't you agree?<br /><br /><b>Magic 8 Ball:</b> Without a doubt.<br /><br /><br />- - - - - -<br /><br />Here are some other reviews to elaborate:<br /><br /> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1101040339?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=2" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a><br /><br /> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1265733533?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=4" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a><br /><br /> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1449218360?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=3" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a> <br /><br /> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1190016156?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=2" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a><br /><br /> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114913907?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=3" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4076905755623390854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3023810070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10400663742725696053">Right now my heart feels like it's gonna explode with happiness!!! (:<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What you loved as a child, you will love forever.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I love this book so. freaking. much!! It has such an interesting premise and such fun and pacy writing it gripped me from the start, which is pretty unusual for me in terms of YA contemporaries. This book is more than 400 pages long but the way I turned the pages one after the other ought to mean that it's a pretty quick read. However, I haven't had much time to rea</span>
  <span id="freeText10400663742725696053" style="display:none">Right now my heart feels like it's gonna explode with happiness!!! (:<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What you loved as a child, you will love forever.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I love this book so. freaking. much!! It has such an interesting premise and such fun and pacy writing it gripped me from the start, which is pretty unusual for me in terms of YA contemporaries. This book is more than 400 pages long but the way I turned the pages one after the other ought to mean that it's a pretty quick read. However, I haven't had much time to read lately and so ended up taking too much time to finish. Just don't worry about that.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The only thing missing was Miles. But he was probably circling somewhere, destroying villages and hoarding gold in his mountain lair.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Alex and Miles have my heart forever. I'm never gonna forget the way Alex describes Miles, especially during the first 3/4th of the book!! It's just too hilarious and cute!!! I loved their club and Charlie and Tucker, too. Even, Ohio! And that epilogue. OMG I don't think there could've been a more suitable ending to a story like that! Schizophrenia isn't something you could cure permanently and I didn't know what to expect and what to not from the last few chapters. I had grown so fond of Alex I didn't want to even think about anything gloomy. So, I got really very scared for her and the fate of her relationship with Miles and all her new-found friendships. Now I thank the Almighty for that epilogue!! T_T<br /><br />So, I loved every single bit of this book. And when I love a book this much I tend to have difficulty expressing myself. So, that's it for now.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17395074384673761841"><br/><b>
  <i>"You're Jetta."<br/>He shook his head.<br/>I frowned. "Theo?"<br/>"No."<br/>"Well if you're not either of them, you'd have to be me."<br/>He blinked. <br/>"It's me?" I said.<br/>"I couldn't think of anyone else," he said.</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/>So....to keep pace with my current obsession of flawed and/or tortured characters and unreliable narrators, I just <b>had</b> to read this. I can't even begin to imagine living in a world where I don't know what's real and what isn't. It's just unfathomable, to me. To look on my desk and see a spider, only to immedi</span>
  <span id="freeText17395074384673761841" style="display:none"><br><b>
  <i>"You're Jetta."<br>He shook his head.<br>I frowned. "Theo?"<br>"No."<br>"Well if you're not either of them, you'd have to be me."<br>He blinked. <br>"It's me?" I said.<br>"I couldn't think of anyone else," he said.</i>
</b><br><br><br>So....to keep pace with my current obsession of flawed and/or tortured characters and unreliable narrators, I just <b>had</b> to read this. I can't even begin to imagine living in a world where I don't know what's real and what isn't. It's just unfathomable, to me. To look on my desk and see a spider, only to immediately think, 'Wait wait wait...is this an <i>actual</i> spider...or am I just imagining it?' That would surely be the end of me. But just ponder this: <b>Nothing is certain, no one is guaranteed to be real, and you might never know if what you're seeing is actually truly happening.</b> How terrifying is <i>that</i>?<br><br><br><b>Was everything made up? Was this whole world inside my head? If I ever woke up from it, would I be inside a padded room somewhere, drooling all over myself?<br>Would I even <i>be</i> myself?</b><br><br><br>Now, this really wasn't what I was expecting. But then, I don't know <i>what</i> I was expecting. I have both strong and lukewarm feelings for this one. Let me explain: The characters were so addicting. I couldn't get enough of mean old [tortured] Miles and poor Alex. I knew from the moment these two met that I was hooked. He was surly as shit, and she wasn't going to take his crap like everyone else in the school. And this is what drove me forward from the very beginning. But then on the other hand...for some odd reason that I can't explain, the story just felt so unrealistic to me. Which makes no sense! Of course it didn't!! We are following an unreliable narrator and we don't know what's real and what isn't. <br><br><br><b>"Alex. Wait."<br>I turned back. It was the first time he'd said my name. He held a hand out. "Well played," he said.<br>Oh no. No, we were not doing this. I hadn't spent ten minutes gluing his locker shut just to admit it to him. So I arched my own eyebrow and said, "I don't know what you're talking about."<br>The corners of his lips twisted up right before I walked away.</b><br><br><br>But I don't even think it's that. Maybe it's their high school life. But when have I ever picked up a book and said-'This is so unbelievable.' Never. I never have. Unless the cheese is through the roof and I can't believe a girl could be so stupid, I never say that. No amount of dystopian or fantasy or paranormal could make me say that....<b>So why did this book make me wonder things I never have?</b> And that's where my lack of that last .5 or full star comes from. I can't decide if I liked the surreal feel of the story...or disliked it. <br><br><br><b>"You're going to go up there"-he pointed at the empty bleachers-"and shut up."<br>Was there some kind of law about drop-kicking assholes in the face? Probably. They always had laws against things that really needed to be done.</b><br><br><br>Not often do I say <b>less is more</b>, but due to lack of time and the fact that this story is based on belief of what's real and not real, I think I need to stick by that thought. I fell inexplicably hard for the male lead, Miles, and I think that stems from my current obsession of 'tortured boys with 'tude problems.' There wasn't one minute where I wasn't begging for more of him, just so I could get to the core of why he was just. So. Mean. I wanted and needed to know what made him tic and, most importantly, I needed to see more of his anger-riddled jealousy. Ah yes, Miles dear got extremely jealous on more than one occasion-Though, he'd never admit it. And I have to say-I loved the confused look on his face all the time. It was adorable. And the eyebrow raise!! And lastly-I loved how he always stood up for Alex, even if it didn't look like he was. How he always was there for her and respected her (in his own way, okay) and took care of her. I loved it. He was a mean shit...but he had reasons. You'll have to read to know anything more than that. <br><br><br><b>I really needed Finnegan's Magic 8 Ball. But I could guess what kind of answer it would give me. <i>Ask again later.</i> So freaking noncommittal.</b> <br><br><br>So, that is all. Still not a short review, by any means, but not near as long as they've been running lately, it seems. I think this book will touch many people because it's not an easy topic to write about, nor is it an easy book to find written <i>well.</i> And that's what this was-an excellently written story with deep characters and a meaningful story-line. I will be suggesting it to many, and I can't wait to come back someday and re-read this with an open mind and knowing what is real...and what isn't.<br><br><br><b>
  <i>I don't want you.<br>I don't need you.<br>I don't love you.</i>
</b><br><br><br><br><br><br>For more of my reviews, please visit:<br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a> <u>
  <b></b>

  <span id="freeText1437406271813439455" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>Hey look, it’s another book I read two months ago and never reviewed. Bonus this time – it was a library book (thanks a lot for denying me the ARC, NetGalley!) and my loan expired therefore erasing all of my quotes. Fail. Luckily my old lady brain didn’t sabotage me on this one so I can kind of halfa$$ review it. Lucky again that this is a book where the less said is better because <b>SPOILERS</b> so if this is on your TBR be careful wading too deep into the reviewing pond (and especially the Questions section on GR) or else you might find you need to cut a b*&amp;^#.<br><br><i>Made You Up</i> is the story of Alex’s senior year. Her main goal is to get in to college, but that’s not as simple as it seems when you have a tendency of spotting the local Phoenix when you go outside . . . . <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2d6uptc" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439482014ra/15843567.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There’s also a <i>tiny</i> problem in the form of a boy named Miles – a boy Alex has always positive was just a figment of her imagination . . . . <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=9050ya" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439482014ra/15843566.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Before I even begin, can I pay homage to that cover????<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=10qi4io" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439482014ra/15843569.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Hands down the most gorgeous book I’ve seen this year. I didn’t even need to look at a synopsis before deciding I would be reading this one. (Note to authors – covers are <b>IMPORTANT</b>. A pretty one will sell your books for you – an ugly one will leave them sitting on the rack alone and unwanted.)<br><br>Alright, now to the book. <i>Made You Up</i> might not be the best thing I’ve ever read, but it’s quite a solid debut and earns bonus points for originality. Although this seems like the “year of the crazy” with respect to the vast amount of characters who are battling some sort of mental disorder, I thought this story did a remarkable job of tackling schizophrenia with a wonderful balance of both humor and compassion. It was also a refreshing change of pace when it came to dealing with what it’s really like to fall in love for the first time. (Spoiler alert for those who have yet to experience it: Love doesn’t happen instantly.) If you’re not emotionally vacant like me <i>Made You Up</i> might even make you experience some feely-feels.<br><br>3.5 Stars rounded up for daring to be different than the stereotypical YA.<br></span>

<div id="review_2188190324" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2188190324" />
    <a title="Sue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7377874-sue"><img alt="Sue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594207220p2/7377874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2188190324?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue" href="/user/show/7377874-sue">Sue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7377874-sue?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7377874-sue?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2188190324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16066485318334886360">This was recommended to me a while back. It’s been sitting on my shelf for ages. It’s not the usual kind of writing I enjoy however, because it was recommended over Mental Health week some time ago (which I’m a supporter of) I bought it.<br/><br/>I am slowly trying to get to my own purchased books bit by bit and decided to choose this one.<br/><br/>Like a lot of clinical psychotic mental health illnesses it edges on hallucinations, paranoia, grandious ideas and more.<br/><br/>schizophrenia is of no exception and we see this </span>
  <span id="freeText16066485318334886360" style="display:none">This was recommended to me a while back. It’s been sitting on my shelf for ages. It’s not the usual kind of writing I enjoy however, because it was recommended over Mental Health week some time ago (which I’m a supporter of) I bought it.<br /><br />I am slowly trying to get to my own purchased books bit by bit and decided to choose this one.<br /><br />Like a lot of clinical psychotic mental health illnesses it edges on hallucinations, paranoia, grandious ideas and more.<br /><br />schizophrenia is of no exception and we see this in the main character.<br /><br />It was interesting how the author wrote this book as it’s not as straight forward as I would have thought.<br />I didn’t know what was fact sometimes and what was her hallucinations, that kept me interested.<br /><br />The love interest made it even more overwhelming and decidedly complicated with someone with such an illness.<br /><br />Medication may keep the psychosis at bay, the break through may be short or horrendously inhibiting.<br /><br />What a very good read once I got the angle of the way the author writes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16066485318334886360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yXizQF7MiAkdwnlH2v8MJrRh1Z/R9/w0Z4QXvb6mwDmUUqTrd5iBFRlS8ETPsdzjramKkiSqXzyxTfd4agZA5Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nXDH9RlFHg4kvWZbknbbdHNxDlhX6jD1dLFh7N+eiqjAWtBeMBEXEiAt71iHOAuxarlRVaK3k/2ieIEpCz4KdA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;People say teenagers think they're immortal, and I agree with that. It means striving for what you want most, even when it seems our of your reach, even when everything is working against you.&rdquo;</span>
